Audio captureMicrophone buffer200–500 msVAD-triggered; 1 s audio minimum
Speech recognitionWhisper large-v3300–800 msGPU inference; ~1 s audio
LLM planningGPT-4o API500–1,500 msNetwork + model inference
Action parsing + groundingObject detection lookup50–150 msLocal; uses cached detections
Action server startupROS 2 overhead10–30 msFirst goal only
Total (typical)~1.1–3.0 sAcceptable for non-urgent tasks

A three-second command-to-motion latency is acceptable for household service tasks (fetching items, carrying objects) but is too slow for tasks requiring rapid response to environmental changes. Chapter 13 discusses streaming and predictive execution strategies to reduce this latency for time-critical operations.

12.3 OpenAI Whisper Integration in ROS 2

12.3.1 What Whisper Is

OpenAI Whisper [1] is a transformer-based automatic speech recognition (ASR) system trained on 680,000 hours of multilingual and multitask audio data collected from the web. Unlike prior ASR systems that required extensive fine-tuning on domain-specific data and careful acoustic modeling, Whisper achieves robust transcription across diverse audio conditions — background noise, accents, reverberant environments — without adaptation.

Whisper's architecture is an encoder-decoder transformer. The encoder processes 30-second audio chunks converted to log-Mel spectrograms; the decoder autoregressively predicts text tokens conditioned on the audio encoding. The model is trained on the task of transcription as a text generation problem, with special tokens controlling the language, task type (transcription vs translation), and whether to produce timestamps.

Whisper is available in five sizes, providing a range of accuracy-latency trade-offs:

Model SizeParametersRelative SpeedWord Error Rate (English)Recommended Use
tiny39M32x~8.5%Edge devices, rapid prototyping
base74M16x~6.4%Low-resource embedded systems
small244M6x~4.9%Real-time on mid-range GPU
medium769M2x~3.7%Balanced accuracy/speed
large-v31.55B1x (baseline)~2.7%Production humanoid robots

For a humanoid robot operating in a home or office environment with a good-quality microphone, large-v3 is the appropriate choice. Its 2.7% word error rate under standard conditions degrades gracefully in noise, and on a single NVIDIA GPU the ~600 ms inference time for a 2-second utterance is within the latency budget.

12.3.2 Python: Loading Whisper and Transcribing Audio

The following standalone module handles microphone capture and transcription using the faster-whisper library — a CTranslate2-based reimplementation of Whisper that achieves 2–4x faster inference than the original PyTorch implementation while maintaining identical accuracy.

<h1>whisper_transcriber.py</h1>

<h1>Standalone Whisper transcription module for ROS 2 node integration.</h1> <h1>Requires: pip install faster-whisper pyaudio numpy</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from dataclasses import dataclass, field from typing import Callable, Optional


from faster_whisper import WhisperModel


@dataclass class TranscriptionResult: """A completed transcription with metadata.""" text: str language: str confidence: float          # Mean log-probability of all segments duration_audio_s: float    # Duration of the audio chunk transcribed latency_s: float           # Wall-clock time from end of speech to result


@dataclass class WhisperConfig: """Configuration for the Whisper transcription module.""" model_size: str = "large-v3" device: str = "cuda"              # "cuda" or "cpu" compute_type: str = "float16"     # "float16", "int8_float16", "int8" language: Optional[str] = "en"   # None for auto-detect # Voice Activity Detection (VAD) parameters vad_silence_threshold_s: float = 0.8   # Silence duration to end utterance vad_min_speech_duration_s: float = 0.5 # Minimum utterance length vad_max_utterance_duration_s: float = 15.0  # Max utterance before forced cut # Audio capture parameters sample_rate: int = 16000 channels: int = 1 chunk_size: int = 1024   # Frames per PyAudio buffer


class WhisperTranscriber: """ Real-time speech transcription using Whisper large-v3.


Captures audio from the default microphone, applies voice activity detection (VAD) to segment utterances, and transcribes each utterance asynchronously.


Usage: def on_transcription(result: TranscriptionResult): print(f"Heard: {result.text}")


transcriber = WhisperTranscriber(callback=on_transcription) transcriber.start() # ... robot runs ... transcriber.stop() """


def __init__( self, callback: Callable[[TranscriptionResult], None], config: WhisperConfig = WhisperConfig(), ) -> None: self.callback = callback self.config = config self._running = False self._audio_queue: queue.Queue[np.ndarray] = queue.Queue()


print(f"Loading Whisper {config.model_size} ({config.compute_type})...") self._model = WhisperModel( config.model_size, device=config.device, compute_type=config.compute_type, ) print("Whisper model ready.")


self._pyaudio = pyaudio.PyAudio()


def start(self) -> None: """Start audio capture and transcription threads.""" self._running = True self._capture_thread = threading.Thread( target=self._capture_loop, daemon=True ) self._transcription_thread = threading.Thread( target=self._transcription_loop, daemon=True ) self._capture_thread.start() self._transcription_thread.start()


def stop(self) -> None: """Stop all threads gracefully.""" self._running = False self._capture_thread.join(timeout=2.0) self._transcription_thread.join(timeout=5.0) self._pyaudio.terminate()


def _capture_loop(self) -> None: """ Continuously capture audio and segment it into utterances using simple energy-based VAD. """ cfg = self.config stream = self._pyaudio.open( rate=cfg.sample_rate, channels=cfg.channels, format=pyaudio.paInt16, input=True, frames_per_buffer=cfg.chunk_size, )


utterance_frames: list[bytes] = [] silence_chunks = 0 speaking = False


# Energy threshold: frames with RMS below this are "silence" silence_rms_threshold = 300  # Tune for environment noise floor


chunks_per_second = cfg.sample_rate // cfg.chunk_size silence_chunks_threshold = int( cfg.vad_silence_threshold_s * chunks_per_second ) min_speech_chunks = int( cfg.vad_min_speech_duration_s * chunks_per_second ) max_utterance_chunks = int( cfg.vad_max_utterance_duration_s * chunks_per_second )


try: while self._running: raw = stream.read(cfg.chunk_size, exception_on_overflow=False) # Compute RMS energy of this chunk samples = struct.unpack( f"{cfg.chunk_size}h", raw ) rms = (sum(s  s for s in samples) / cfg.chunk_size) * 0.5 is_speech = rms > silence_rms_threshold


if is_speech: utterance_frames.append(raw) silence_chunks = 0 speaking = True elif speaking: utterance_frames.append(raw) silence_chunks += 1


if silence_chunks >= silence_chunks_threshold: # End of utterance detected if len(utterance_frames) >= min_speech_chunks: audio_bytes = b"".join(utterance_frames) audio_np = np.frombuffer( audio_bytes, dtype=np.int16 ).astype(np.float32) / 32768.0 self._audio_queue.put(audio_np)


utterance_frames = [] silence_chunks = 0 speaking = False elif len(utterance_frames) >= max_utterance_chunks: # Force-cut very long utterances audio_bytes = b"".join(utterance_frames) audio_np = np.frombuffer( audio_bytes, dtype=np.int16 ).astype(np.float32) / 32768.0 self._audio_queue.put(audio_np) utterance_frames = [] speaking = False finally: stream.stop_stream() stream.close()


def _transcription_loop(self) -> None: """ Dequeue captured audio utterances and transcribe them with Whisper. """ cfg = self.config while self._running: try: audio = self._audio_queue.get(timeout=0.5) except queue.Empty: continue


t0 = time.monotonic() duration_s = len(audio) / cfg.sample_rate


segments, info = self._model.transcribe( audio, language=cfg.language, beam_size=5, vad_filter=True,  # Whisper's built-in VAD post-processing vad_parameters={ "min_silence_duration_ms": 500, }, )


text_parts = [] total_logprob = 0.0 segment_count = 0 for segment in segments: text_parts.append(segment.text.strip()) total_logprob += segment.avg_logprob segment_count += 1


if not text_parts: continue


full_text = " ".join(text_parts).strip() avg_logprob = total_logprob / max(segment_count, 1) # Convert avg log-probability to a 0-1 confidence score confidence = float(np.exp(avg_logprob)) latency_s = time.monotonic() - t0


result = TranscriptionResult( text=full_text, language=info.language, confidence=confidence, duration_audio_s=duration_s, latency_s=latency_s, ) self.callback(result)

12.3.3 ROS 2 Node Wrapping Whisper

The WhisperTranscriber module is wrapped in a ROS 2 node that publishes transcribed text to a standard ROS 2 topic for consumption by downstream nodes.

<h1>whisper_node.py</h1>

<h1>ROS 2 node: microphone → Whisper → /speech/transcription topic</h1> <h1>Requires: ros2 humble, pip install faster-whisper pyaudio</h1> <h1>Run: ros2 run voice_pipeline whisper_node</h1>


from rclpy.node import Node from std_msgs.msg import String from voice_pipeline.whisper_transcriber import ( WhisperTranscriber, WhisperConfig, TranscriptionResult, )


class WhisperNode(Node): """ ROS 2 node that captures speech from the microphone, transcribes it using Whisper large-v3, and publishes the text to /speech/transcription.


Published Topics: /speech/transcription  (std_msgs/String)  — Raw transcribed text /speech/confidence     (std_msgs/Float32) — Transcription confidence """


def __init__(self) -> None: super().__init__("whisper_node")


# Declare ROS 2 parameters (overridable via launch file or CLI) self.declare_parameter("model_size", "large-v3") self.declare_parameter("language", "en") self.declare_parameter("device", "cuda") self.declare_parameter("confidence_threshold", 0.6)


model_size = self.get_parameter("model_size").value language = self.get_parameter("language").value device = self.get_parameter("device").value self._confidence_threshold = self.get_parameter( "confidence_threshold" ).value


# Publishers self._transcription_pub = self.create_publisher( String, "/speech/transcription", qos_profile=10 )


# Start transcription in background thread config = WhisperConfig( model_size=model_size, language=language if language != "auto" else None, device=device, ) self._transcriber = WhisperTranscriber( callback=self._on_transcription, config=config, ) self._transcriber.start()


self.get_logger().info( f"WhisperNode ready. Model: {model_size}, " f"Language: {language}, Device: {device}" )


def _on_transcription(self, result: TranscriptionResult) -> None: """Callback invoked by the transcription thread when text is ready.""" self.get_logger().info( f"Transcribed ({result.confidence:.2f}): '{result.text}' " f"[{result.latency_s:.2f}s latency]" )


if result.confidence < self._confidence_threshold: self.get_logger().warn( f"Low confidence ({result.confidence:.2f}), discarding: " f"'{result.text}'" ) return


msg = String() msg.data = result.text self._transcription_pub.publish(msg)


def destroy_node(self) -> None: self._transcriber.stop() super().destroy_node()


def main(args=None) -> None: rclpy.init(args=args) node = WhisperNode() try: rclpy.spin(node) except KeyboardInterrupt: pass finally: node.destroy_node() rclpy.shutdown()


if __name__ == "__main__": main()

12.4 LLM Task Planning with GPT-4o

12.4.1 System Prompt Design for Robot Task Planning

GPT-4o receives the transcribed instruction and must convert it into a structured, executable action plan. The quality of this conversion depends critically on the system prompt — the instructions that constrain GPT-4o's output format, robot capabilities, and reasoning process.

The system prompt must communicate:

  1. The robot's physical capabilities (what actions it can perform)
  2. The objects currently visible to the robot (from the perception system)
  3. The output format (a JSON structure the parser can process)
  4. Constraint checking (feasibility, safety)

12.4.2 Pydantic Models for Structured Robot Actions

Pydantic [4] models define the schema for robot action plans, providing type safety and automatic validation of GPT-4o's structured outputs.

<h1>robot_action_schema.py</h1>

<h1>Pydantic v2 models defining the structured output schema for robot actions.</h1> <h1>Requires: pip install pydantic>=2.0 openai>=1.0</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from enum import Enum from typing import Optional from pydantic import BaseModel, Field, model_validator


class ActionType(str, Enum): """Enumeration of all executable robot action primitives.""" NAVIGATE_TO = "navigate_to"   # Move robot base to a position PICK_UP = "pick_up"           # Grasp an object PLACE = "place"               # Place held object at location SPEAK = "speak"               # Text-to-speech output WAIT = "wait"                 # Pause for specified duration OPEN_DOOR = "open_door"       # Open a door (requires door handle detection) POUR = "pour"                 # Pour contents (liquid tasks)


class RobotAction(BaseModel): """A single executable robot action primitive."""


action_type: ActionType = Field( description="The type of action to execute." ) target_object: Optional[str] = Field( default=None, description=( "The name of the target object for this action, as it appears " "in the detected_objects list provided in the system prompt." ), ) target_location: Optional[str] = Field( default=None, description=( "The name of a named location (e.g., 'kitchen counter', " "'user_position') or a detected object to navigate/place to." ), ) text_to_speak: Optional[str] = Field( default=None, description="The text to say aloud (for SPEAK actions only).", ) duration_s: Optional[float] = Field( default=None, ge=0.1, le=30.0, description="Duration in seconds (for WAIT actions only).", ) notes: Optional[str] = Field( default=None, description="Brief reasoning note explaining why this step is needed.", )


@model_validator(mode="after") def validate_action_fields(self) -> "RobotAction": """Ensure required fields are present for each action type.""" if self.action_type in (ActionType.PICK_UP, ActionType.POUR): if not self.target_object: raise ValueError( f"{self.action_type} requires target_object" ) if self.action_type == ActionType.NAVIGATE_TO: if not self.target_location and not self.target_object: raise ValueError( "NAVIGATE_TO requires target_location or target_object" ) if self.action_type == ActionType.PLACE: if not self.target_location and not self.target_object: raise ValueError( "PLACE requires target_location or target_object" ) if self.action_type == ActionType.SPEAK: if not self.text_to_speak: raise ValueError("SPEAK requires text_to_speak") if self.action_type == ActionType.WAIT: if self.duration_s is None: raise ValueError("WAIT requires duration_s") return self


class ActionPlan(BaseModel): """ A complete, ordered plan for executing a voice-commanded robot task. """


task_description: str = Field( description="One-sentence description of the overall task." ) feasible: bool = Field( description=( "True if all required objects/locations are detected and " "the task is physically achievable. False otherwise." ) ) infeasibility_reason: Optional[str] = Field( default=None, description="If feasible=False, explain why the task cannot be done.", ) steps: list[RobotAction] = Field( default_factory=list, description=( "Ordered list of robot action primitives to execute. " "Empty if feasible=False." ), ) estimated_duration_s: Optional[float] = Field( default=None, description="Estimated total task duration in seconds.", )


@model_validator(mode="after") def validate_plan(self) -> "ActionPlan": if not self.feasible and not self.infeasibility_reason: raise ValueError( "infeasibility_reason is required when feasible=False" ) if self.feasible and not self.steps: raise ValueError( "steps must be non-empty when feasible=True" ) return self

12.4.3 GPT-4o Task Planning Node

<h1>gpt4o_planner_node.py</h1>

<h1>ROS 2 node: /speech/transcription → GPT-4o → /task/action_plan</h1> <h1>Requires: pip install openai>=1.0 pydantic>=2.0</h1> <h1>Environment: OPENAI_API_KEY must be set</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from typing import Optional


from rclpy.node import Node from std_msgs.msg import String from openai import OpenAI


from voice_pipeline.robot_action_schema import ActionPlan, ActionType


<h1>System prompt template. The {detected_objects} placeholder is filled</h1> <h1>at runtime with the current list of detected objects from the perception system.</h1> SYSTEM_PROMPT_TEMPLATE = """You are the task planning module for a humanoid service robot.


<h2>Robot Capabilities</h2> The robot can execute the following action primitives:


  • navigate_to: Move the robot base to a named location or detected object
  • pick_up: Grasp a detected object with the robot arm
  • place: Place the currently held object at a named location or near a detected object
  • speak: Say text aloud via the robot's text-to-speech system
  • wait: Pause for a specified number of seconds
  • open_door: Open a door (only if a door handle is visible)
  • pour: Pour the contents of a held container


<h2>Currently Detected Objects</h2> The robot's perception system currently detects the following objects: {detected_objects}


<h2>Named Locations</h2> {named_locations}


<h2>Instructions</h2>


  1. Convert the user's voice command into an ordered list of action primitives.
  2. Use ONLY objects from the detected objects list. Do NOT assume objects are present if not listed.
  3. If the task is impossible (required object not detected, physically infeasible), set feasible=False.
  4. If the command is ambiguous, produce a SPEAK action asking for clarification, then set feasible=False.
  5. Always include a SPEAK action at the start to confirm understanding of the task.
  6. Always include a SPEAK action at the end to report completion or failure.
  7. Respond ONLY with valid JSON matching the ActionPlan schema.
"""

class GPT4oPlannerNode(Node): """ ROS 2 node that subscribes to transcribed speech, queries GPT-4o to generate a structured action plan, and publishes the plan as JSON.


Subscribed Topics: /speech/transcription (std_msgs/String)  — Transcribed voice command /perception/objects   (std_msgs/String)  — JSON list of detected objects


Published Topics: /task/action_plan     (std_msgs/String)  — JSON ActionPlan """


def __init__(self) -> None: super().__init__("gpt4o_planner_node")


self.declare_parameter("model", "gpt-4o") self.declare_parameter("temperature", 0.1) self.declare_parameter("max_tokens", 1024)


self._model = self.get_parameter("model").value self._temperature = self.get_parameter("temperature").value self._max_tokens = self.get_parameter("max_tokens").value


api_key = os.environ.get("OPENAI_API_KEY") if not api_key: raise RuntimeError( "OPENAI_API_KEY environment variable is not set." ) self._client = OpenAI(api_key=api_key)


# Current detected objects (updated by perception subscription) self._detected_objects: list[str] = [] self._named_locations: list[str] = [ "kitchen_counter", "dining_table", "user_position", "charging_station", "storage_shelf", ]


self._transcription_sub = self.create_subscription( String, "/speech/transcription", self._on_transcription, 10 ) self._objects_sub = self.create_subscription( String, "/perception/objects", self._on_objects_update, 10 ) self._plan_pub = self.create_publisher( String, "/task/action_plan", 10 )


self.get_logger().info("GPT4oPlannerNode ready.")


def _on_objects_update(self, msg: String) -> None: """Update the list of currently detected objects.""" try: self._detected_objects = json.loads(msg.data) except json.JSONDecodeError as e: self.get_logger().error(f"Failed to parse objects list: {e}")


def _on_transcription(self, msg: String) -> None: """Handle a new transcribed voice command.""" instruction = msg.data.strip() if not instruction: return


self.get_logger().info(f"Planning task for: '{instruction}'")


# Format detected objects as a readable list for the prompt if self._detected_objects: objects_str = "\n".join( f"  - {obj}" for obj in self._detected_objects ) else: objects_str = "  (no objects currently detected)"


locations_str = "\n".join( f"  - {loc}" for loc in self._named_locations )


system_prompt = SYSTEM_PROMPT_TEMPLATE.format( detected_objects=objects_str, named_locations=locations_str, )


try: action_plan = self._call_gpt4o(system_prompt, instruction) plan_json = action_plan.model_dump_json(indent=2)


self.get_logger().info( f"Plan generated: {action_plan.task_description} " f"(feasible={action_plan.feasible}, " f"steps={len(action_plan.steps)})" )


plan_msg = String() plan_msg.data = plan_json self._plan_pub.publish(plan_msg)


except Exception as e: self.get_logger().error(f"GPT-4o planning failed: {e}") # Publish a fallback "speak clarification" plan fallback = ActionPlan( task_description="Planning failure", feasible=False, infeasibility_reason=str(e), steps=[], ) plan_msg = String() plan_msg.data = fallback.model_dump_json() self._plan_pub.publish(plan_msg)


def _call_gpt4o(self, system_prompt: str, instruction: str) -> ActionPlan: """Call GPT-4o with structured JSON output and parse into ActionPlan.""" response = self._client.chat.completions.create( model=self._model, temperature=self._temperature, max_tokens=self._max_tokens, response_format={"type": "json_object"}, messages=[ {"role": "system", "content": system_prompt}, {"role": "user", "content": instruction}, ], )


raw_json = response.choices[0].message.content data = json.loads(raw_json) # Validate and construct the ActionPlan with Pydantic return ActionPlan.model_validate(data)


def main(args=None) -> None: rclpy.init(args=args) node = GPT4oPlannerNode() try: rclpy.spin(node) except KeyboardInterrupt: pass finally: node.destroy_node() rclpy.shutdown()


if __name__ == "__main__": main()

12.4.4 Example: "Bring Me the Red Mug" → Structured Action Plan

Given the instruction "bring me the red mug" with the detected objects list ["red_mug", "coffee_maker", "kitchen_counter"] and the user at user_position, GPT-4o would generate the following structured plan:

{

"task_description": "Pick up the red mug and bring it to the user.", "feasible": true, "infeasibility_reason": null, "steps": [ { "action_type": "speak", "text_to_speak": "Sure, I'll bring you the red mug.", "notes": "Confirm task understanding" }, { "action_type": "navigate_to", "target_object": "red_mug", "notes": "Move base close to the mug's detected position" }, { "action_type": "pick_up", "target_object": "red_mug", "notes": "Grasp the red mug" }, { "action_type": "navigate_to", "target_location": "user_position", "notes": "Return to user with the mug" }, { "action_type": "place", "target_location": "user_position", "notes": "Offer the mug to the user" }, { "action_type": "speak", "text_to_speak": "Here is your red mug.", "notes": "Report task completion" } ], "estimated_duration_s": 45.0 }

12.5 Grounding Language Commands to Robot State

12.5.1 The Grounding Problem

GPT-4o produces plans that refer to objects by name: "red_mug," "kitchen_counter." But a robot does not act on names — it acts on poses: 3D positions and orientations in the robot's coordinate frame. The process of converting a named object reference into a concrete spatial pose is called grounding.

The grounding problem has two levels:

Perceptual grounding: "red_mug" must be mapped to a bounding box in the camera image, then to a 3D point cloud cluster, then to a grasp pose. This requires integration with the object detection system described in Chapter 9. Spatial language grounding: Phrases like "to the left of the coffee maker" or "on the table near the window" require spatial reasoning — computing a 3D position that satisfies the described spatial relationship relative to detected reference objects.

12.5.2 Python: Grounding a Detected Object to a Pose

<h1>action_grounding.py</h1>

<h1>Grounds named object references in an ActionPlan to concrete 3D poses.</h1> <h1>Integrates with the object detection system via the /perception/detections topic.</h1> <h1>Requires: pip install numpy scipy</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from dataclasses import dataclass from typing import Optional


@dataclass class ObjectDetection: """A single detected object with 3D pose in the robot's base frame.""" label: str confidence: float position_xyz: np.ndarray   # shape (3,), meters in robot base frame orientation_quat: np.ndarray   # shape (4,), [x, y, z, w] bounding_box_2d: tuple[int, int, int, int]  # (x1, y1, x2, y2) pixels


@dataclass class GroundedPose: """A resolved 3D pose for an action target.""" position_xyz: np.ndarray     # shape (3,) orientation_quat: np.ndarray # shape (4,) source_label: str confidence: float


class ActionGrounder: """ Resolves named object/location references from an ActionPlan to 3D poses.


The grounding process: 1. For object references (e.g., "red_mug"): look up the detected object with matching label and highest confidence. 2. For spatial language (e.g., "left of coffee_maker"): compute position relative to the reference object. 3. For named locations (e.g., "user_position"): look up in a static map. """


def __init__(self, static_locations: dict[str, np.ndarray]) -> None: """ Args: static_locations: Map of location name -> (x, y, z) in base frame. e.g. {"user_position": np.array([2.0, 0.0, 0.0])} """ self._static_locations = static_locations self._current_detections: list[ObjectDetection] = []


def update_detections(self, detections: list[ObjectDetection]) -> None: """Update the cache of currently detected objects.""" self._current_detections = detections


def ground_object(self, object_label: str) -> Optional[GroundedPose]: """ Ground a named object to its 3D pose in the robot's base frame.


Returns None if the object is not currently detected. """ matches = [ det for det in self._current_detections if det.label.lower() == object_label.lower() ] if not matches: return None


# Select the detection with highest confidence best = max(matches, key=lambda d: d.confidence)


return GroundedPose( position_xyz=best.position_xyz.copy(), orientation_quat=best.orientation_quat.copy(), source_label=best.label, confidence=best.confidence, )


def ground_location(self, location_name: str) -> Optional[GroundedPose]: """ Ground a named location to a 3D pose.


First tries detected objects (a named location might be a large object like "kitchen_counter"), then falls back to the static location map. """ # Try treating the location name as a detected object first grounded = self.ground_object(location_name) if grounded is not None: return grounded


# Fall back to static map if location_name in self._static_locations: xyz = self._static_locations[location_name] return GroundedPose( position_xyz=xyz.copy(), orientation_quat=np.array([0.0, 0.0, 0.0, 1.0]), source_label=location_name, confidence=1.0, )


return None


def ground_spatial_expression( self, reference_label: str, relation: str, offset_m: float = 0.3, ) -> Optional[GroundedPose]: """ Ground a spatial expression like "to the left of {reference_label}".


Supported relations: "left_of", "right_of", "in_front_of", "behind", "above", "below"


Args: reference_label: Label of the reference object relation:         Spatial relation string offset_m:         Distance offset in meters from reference object


Returns: GroundedPose at the computed spatial position, or None. """ ref = self.ground_object(reference_label) if ref is None: return None


# Compute offset direction in robot base frame # Assumes robot is facing the +x direction relation_offsets = { "left_of":     np.array([0.0,  offset_m, 0.0]), "right_of":    np.array([0.0, -offset_m, 0.0]), "in_front_of": np.array([offset_m, 0.0, 0.0]), "behind":      np.array([-offset_m, 0.0, 0.0]), "above":       np.array([0.0, 0.0, offset_m]), "below":       np.array([0.0, 0.0, -offset_m]), }


if relation not in relation_offsets: return None


new_position = ref.position_xyz + relation_offsets[relation]


return GroundedPose( position_xyz=new_position, orientation_quat=ref.orientation_quat.copy(), source_label=f"{relation}_{reference_label}", confidence=ref.confidence * 0.9,  # Slightly lower confidence )

12.6 ROS 2 Action Server for Task Execution

12.6.1 The ROS 2 Action Interface

ROS 2 actions [5] are the appropriate communication pattern for long-running robot tasks. Unlike services (which are synchronous request-response) or topics (which are asynchronous publish-subscribe), actions support three critical features for robot task execution:

  1. Goal acceptance/rejection: The server can reject a goal before starting execution
  2. Feedback streaming: The server publishes periodic progress updates during execution
  3. Cancellation: The client can cancel a goal mid-execution with a graceful response

12.6.2 The ExecuteTask Action Definition

ROS 2 action definitions are stored in .action files in the package's action/ directory. The following file defines the ExecuteTask action interface:

<h1>action/ExecuteTask.action</h1>

<h1>Goal: the full action plan as a JSON string</h1> string plan_json




<h1>Result: success/failure and summary message</h1> bool success string result_message string[] completed_steps string[] failed_steps




<h1>Feedback: step-by-step progress updates</h1> string current_step string current_action_type float32 progress_fraction   # 0.0 to 1.0 string status_message

This action file is placed at voice_pipeline/action/ExecuteTask.action and referenced in CMakeLists.txt (for C++ packages) or setup.py (for Python packages) to generate the message types.

12.6.3 Complete ROS 2 Action Server

<h1>task_executor_server.py</h1>

<h1>ROS 2 Action Server that executes structured ActionPlan objects.</h1> <h1>Implements NavigateTo, PickUp, Place, Speak, and Wait primitives.</h1> <h1>Requires: ros2 humble</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from typing import Optional


from rclpy.action import ActionServer, CancelResponse, GoalResponse from rclpy.action.server import ServerGoalHandle from rclpy.callback_groups import ReentrantCallbackGroup from rclpy.node import Node


<h1>These message types are generated from ExecuteTask.action</h1> from voice_pipeline_interfaces.action import ExecuteTask from voice_pipeline.robot_action_schema import ActionPlan, ActionType from voice_pipeline.action_grounding import ActionGrounder, ObjectDetection


class TaskExecutorServer(Node): """ ROS 2 Action Server that executes structured robot task plans.


Accepts ExecuteTask goals containing a JSON ActionPlan, executes each step sequentially, publishes progress feedback, and handles cancellation and error recovery.


Action Interface: /execute_task (voice_pipeline_interfaces/ExecuteTask) """


def __init__(self) -> None: super().__init__("task_executor_server")


# Grounding module (static locations set at startup) static_locs = { "user_position":    np.array([2.0, 0.0, 0.9]), "kitchen_counter":  np.array([3.5, 1.2, 0.85]), "dining_table":     np.array([1.5, -2.0, 0.75]), "charging_station": np.array([-1.0, 0.0, 0.0]), } self._grounder = ActionGrounder(static_locations=static_locs)


# Action server with reentrant callback group to allow cancellation self._action_server = ActionServer( self, ExecuteTask, "/execute_task", execute_callback=self._execute_callback, goal_callback=self._goal_callback, cancel_callback=self._cancel_callback, callback_group=ReentrantCallbackGroup(), )


self.get_logger().info("TaskExecutorServer ready on /execute_task")


def _goal_callback(self, goal_request) -> GoalResponse: """Validate and accept or reject incoming goals.""" try: plan = ActionPlan.model_validate_json(goal_request.plan_json) if not plan.feasible: self.get_logger().warn( f"Rejecting infeasible goal: {plan.infeasibility_reason}" ) return GoalResponse.REJECT self.get_logger().info( f"Accepting goal: {plan.task_description} " f"({len(plan.steps)} steps)" ) return GoalResponse.ACCEPT except Exception as e: self.get_logger().error(f"Goal validation failed: {e}") return GoalResponse.REJECT


def _cancel_callback(self, goal_handle) -> CancelResponse: """Accept all cancellation requests.""" self.get_logger().info("Cancellation requested — accepting.") return CancelResponse.ACCEPT


async def _execute_callback( self, goal_handle: ServerGoalHandle ) -> ExecuteTask.Result: """ Main execution loop: iterate through ActionPlan steps and execute each. """ plan = ActionPlan.model_validate_json(goal_handle.request.plan_json) completed_steps: list[str] = [] failed_steps: list[str] = [] total_steps = len(plan.steps)


self.get_logger().info( f"Executing: '{plan.task_description}' ({total_steps} steps)" )


for step_idx, action in enumerate(plan.steps): # Check for cancellation before each step if goal_handle.is_cancel_requested: self.get_logger().info("Goal cancelled during execution.") goal_handle.canceled() result = ExecuteTask.Result() result.success = False result.result_message = "Task cancelled by user." result.completed_steps = completed_steps result.failed_steps = [a.action_type.value for a in plan.steps[step_idx:]] return result


# Publish feedback feedback = ExecuteTask.Feedback() feedback.current_step = f"Step {step_idx + 1} of {total_steps}" feedback.current_action_type = action.action_type.value feedback.progress_fraction = step_idx / total_steps feedback.status_message = ( f"Executing {action.action_type.value}" + (f" on {action.target_object}" if action.target_object else "") ) goal_handle.publish_feedback(feedback)


# Execute the action primitive success = await self._execute_action(action)


if success: completed_steps.append(action.action_type.value) self.get_logger().info( f"  Step {step_idx + 1}/{total_steps} OK: " f"{action.action_type.value}" ) else: failed_steps.append(action.action_type.value) self.get_logger().error( f"  Step {step_idx + 1}/{total_steps} FAILED: " f"{action.action_type.value}" )


# Attempt graceful recovery: announce failure and stop await self._speak( f"I encountered an error during step " f"{step_idx + 1}: {action.action_type.value}. " f"Please check the robot's position." )


goal_handle.abort() result = ExecuteTask.Result() result.success = False result.result_message = ( f"Failed at step {step_idx + 1}: {action.action_type.value}" ) result.completed_steps = completed_steps result.failed_steps = failed_steps return result


# All steps completed goal_handle.succeed() result = ExecuteTask.Result() result.success = True result.result_message = f"Task completed: {plan.task_description}" result.completed_steps = completed_steps result.failed_steps = [] return result


async def _execute_action(self, action) -> bool: """ Dispatch a single action primitive to the appropriate handler. Returns True on success, False on failure. """ handlers = { ActionType.NAVIGATE_TO: self._execute_navigate, ActionType.PICK_UP:     self._execute_pick_up, ActionType.PLACE:       self._execute_place, ActionType.SPEAK:       self._execute_speak_action, ActionType.WAIT:        self._execute_wait, }


handler = handlers.get(action.action_type) if handler is None: self.get_logger().warn( f"No handler for action type: {action.action_type}" ) return False


try: return await handler(action) except Exception as e: self.get_logger().error( f"Exception in handler for {action.action_type}: {e}" ) return False


async def _execute_navigate(self, action) -> bool: """Navigate the robot base to the target location or object.""" target = action.target_location or action.target_object pose = self._grounder.ground_location(target) if pose is None: self.get_logger().error(f"Cannot ground location: {target}") return False


self.get_logger().info( f"  Navigating to {target} at " f"({pose.position_xyz[0]:.2f}, " f"{pose.position_xyz[1]:.2f}, " f"{pose.position_xyz[2]:.2f})" ) # In production: call nav2 navigate_to_pose action server here # nav2_client.send_goal(pose) and await result await self._simulate_action(duration_s=3.0)  # Placeholder return True


async def _execute_pick_up(self, action) -> bool: """Grasp the target object.""" pose = self._grounder.ground_object(action.target_object) if pose is None: self.get_logger().error( f"Cannot ground object for pick_up: {action.target_object}" ) return False


self.get_logger().info( f"  Picking up {action.target_object} at " f"({pose.position_xyz[0]:.2f}, " f"{pose.position_xyz[1]:.2f}, " f"{pose.position_xyz[2]:.2f})" ) # In production: call manipulation action server (MoveIt2 or VLA) await self._simulate_action(duration_s=5.0)  # Placeholder return True


async def _execute_place(self, action) -> bool: """Place the held object at the target location.""" target = action.target_location or action.target_object pose = self._grounder.ground_location(target) if pose is None: self.get_logger().error(f"Cannot ground place location: {target}") return False


self.get_logger().info(f"  Placing at {target}") await self._simulate_action(duration_s=3.0)  # Placeholder return True


async def _execute_speak_action(self, action) -> bool: """Speak text aloud via TTS.""" return await self._speak(action.text_to_speak)


async def _speak(self, text: str) -> bool: """Text-to-speech output.""" self.get_logger().info(f'  SPEAK: "{text}"') # In production: call TTS service (e.g., espeak, pyttsx3, ElevenLabs) await self._simulate_action(duration_s=len(text) * 0.05) return True


async def _execute_wait(self, action) -> bool: """Wait for the specified duration.""" self.get_logger().info(f"  Waiting {action.duration_s:.1f}s") await self._simulate_action(duration_s=action.duration_s) return True


async def _simulate_action(self, duration_s: float) -> None: """ Placeholder: simulate action execution with a sleep. Replace with real hardware calls in production. """ import asyncio await asyncio.sleep(duration_s)


def main(args=None) -> None: rclpy.init(args=args) node = TaskExecutorServer() try: rclpy.spin(node) except KeyboardInterrupt: pass finally: node.destroy_node() rclpy.shutdown()


if __name__ == "__main__": main()

12.7 Error Handling

12.7.1 Ambiguous Commands: Requesting Clarification

When GPT-4o determines that a command is ambiguous — "bring me the mug" when two mugs are detected — the planned response is a SPEAK action followed by feasible=False. The action server receives an infeasible plan and instead of executing it, the TTS system speaks the clarification question to the user:

<h1>In GPT4oPlannerNode._on_transcription, for infeasible plans:</h1>

if not plan.feasible: # Generate a clarification request clarification = self._generate_clarification(plan) tts_msg = String() tts_msg.data = clarification self._tts_pub.publish(tts_msg)

GPT-4o's clarification is embedded in the speak step's text_to_speak field: "I see two mugs — a red one and a blue one. Which would you like?"

12.7.2 Impossible Tasks: Graceful Refusal

When a required object is not detected — "bring me the newspaper" when no newspaper is in the scene — GPT-4o sets feasible=False with infeasibility_reason="newspaper not in detected objects list". The pipeline speaks this reason aloud in a user-friendly formulation: "I'm sorry, I don't see a newspaper in the area. Please show me where it is."

12.7.3 Physical Failure and Timeout Handling

Physical failures — a failed grasp, a navigation timeout, a collision — are detected at the action server level. Each action handler wraps its hardware call in a try/except with a configurable timeout:

async def _execute_with_timeout(

self, coro, timeout_s: float, action_name: str, ) -> bool: """Execute an action coroutine with a timeout.""" import asyncio try: result = await asyncio.wait_for(coro, timeout=timeout_s) return result except asyncio.TimeoutError: self.get_logger().error( f"{action_name} timed out after {timeout_s:.1f}s" ) return False except Exception as e: self.get_logger().error(f"{action_name} raised exception: {e}") return False

Recovery behaviors include: backing up to a safe standoff distance after a failed grasp, returning to the home position after a navigation failure, and speaking an error message before stopping.

12.8 Full Capstone Pipeline — Complete Working Example

12.8.1 Package Structure

voice_pipeline/

├── voice_pipeline/ │   ├── __init__.py │   ├── whisper_transcriber.py      # WhisperTranscriber class │   ├── whisper_node.py             # ROS 2 Whisper node │   ├── robot_action_schema.py      # Pydantic models │   ├── gpt4o_planner_node.py       # GPT-4o planner node │   ├── action_grounding.py         # ActionGrounder class │   ├── action_parser_node.py       # Action parser + grounding node │   └── task_executor_server.py     # ROS 2 action server ├── action/ │   └── ExecuteTask.action          # Action definition file ├── launch/ │   └── voice_pipeline.launch.py    # Full pipeline launch file ├── package.xml └── setup.py

12.8.2 The Action Parser Node

The action parser node bridges the GPT-4o planner and the task executor: it receives the JSON ActionPlan, grounds all object and location references to 3D poses, and sends the grounded plan as a goal to the ExecuteTask action server.

<h1>action_parser_node.py</h1>

<h1>ROS 2 node: /task/action_plan -> grounding -> /execute_task goal</h1> <h1>Subscribes to action plans, grounds them, sends to executor.</h1>


from __future__ import annotations


from rclpy.action import ActionClient from rclpy.node import Node from std_msgs.msg import String


from voice_pipeline_interfaces.action import ExecuteTask from voice_pipeline.robot_action_schema import ActionPlan from voice_pipeline.action_grounding import ActionGrounder, ObjectDetection


class ActionParserNode(Node): """ ROS 2 node that receives ActionPlan JSON, validates grounding, and sends the plan as a goal to the TaskExecutorServer.


Subscribed Topics: /task/action_plan    (std_msgs/String) — JSON ActionPlan from GPT-4o /perception/objects  (std_msgs/String) — Detected objects with poses


Action Client: /execute_task (voice_pipeline_interfaces/ExecuteTask) """


def __init__(self) -> None: super().__init__("action_parser_node")


static_locs = { "user_position":    np.array([2.0, 0.0, 0.9]), "kitchen_counter":  np.array([3.5, 1.2, 0.85]), "dining_table":     np.array([1.5, -2.0, 0.75]), "charging_station": np.array([-1.0, 0.0, 0.0]), } self._grounder = ActionGrounder(static_locations=static_locs) self._current_detections: list[ObjectDetection] = []


self._plan_sub = self.create_subscription( String, "/task/action_plan", self._on_plan, 10 ) self._objects_sub = self.create_subscription( String, "/perception/objects_with_poses", self._on_objects_update, 10 ) self._action_client = ActionClient( self, ExecuteTask, "/execute_task" )


self.get_logger().info("ActionParserNode ready.")


def _on_objects_update(self, msg: String) -> None: """Update detections cache from the perception system.""" try: raw = json.loads(msg.data) detections = [] for obj in raw: det = ObjectDetection( label=obj["label"], confidence=obj["confidence"], position_xyz=np.array(obj["position_xyz"]), orientation_quat=np.array(obj["orientation_quat"]), bounding_box_2d=tuple(obj["bbox"]), ) detections.append(det) self._grounder.update_detections(detections) except (json.JSONDecodeError, KeyError) as e: self.get_logger().error(f"Failed to parse detections: {e}")


def _on_plan(self, msg: String) -> None: """Receive a plan and validate grounding before execution.""" try: plan = ActionPlan.model_validate_json(msg.data) except Exception as e: self.get_logger().error(f"Failed to parse ActionPlan: {e}") return


if not plan.feasible: self.get_logger().warn( f"Plan is infeasible: {plan.infeasibility_reason}" ) return


# Validate that all referenced objects/locations can be grounded unresolvable = [] for step in plan.steps: if step.target_object: if not self._grounder.ground_object(step.target_object): unresolvable.append(step.target_object) if step.target_location: if not self._grounder.ground_location(step.target_location): unresolvable.append(step.target_location)


if unresolvable: self.get_logger().error( f"Cannot ground references: {unresolvable}. Aborting." ) return


# Send the validated plan to the action server self.get_logger().info( f"Sending plan to executor: {plan.task_description}" ) if not self._action_client.wait_for_server(timeout_sec=5.0): self.get_logger().error("ExecuteTask action server not available.") return


goal = ExecuteTask.Goal() goal.plan_json = msg.data future = self._action_client.send_goal_async( goal, feedback_callback=self._on_feedback, ) future.add_done_callback(self._on_goal_response)


def _on_goal_response(self, future) -> None: goal_handle = future.result() if not goal_handle.accepted: self.get_logger().error("Goal rejected by executor.") return self.get_logger().info("Goal accepted. Execution in progress...") result_future = goal_handle.get_result_async() result_future.add_done_callback(self._on_result)


def _on_feedback(self, feedback_msg) -> None: fb = feedback_msg.feedback self.get_logger().info( f"[{fb.progress_fraction*100:.0f}%] " f"{fb.current_step}: {fb.status_message}" )


def _on_result(self, future) -> None: result = future.result().result if result.success: self.get_logger().info( f"Task completed: {result.result_message}" ) else: self.get_logger().error( f"Task failed: {result.result_message}" )


def main(args=None) -> None: rclpy.init(args=args) node = ActionParserNode() try: rclpy.spin(node) except KeyboardInterrupt: pass finally: node.destroy_node() rclpy.shutdown()


if __name__ == "__main__": main()

12.8.3 Launch File: Starting the Complete Pipeline

<h1>launch/voice_pipeline.launch.py</h1>

<h1>Launches all four nodes of the voice-to-action pipeline.</h1> <h1>Usage: ros2 launch voice_pipeline voice_pipeline.launch.py</h1>


from launch import LaunchDescription from launch.actions import DeclareLaunchArgument, LogInfo from launch.substitutions import LaunchConfiguration from launch_ros.actions import Node


def generate_launch_description() -> LaunchDescription: """ Launch all voice pipeline nodes with configurable parameters.


Nodes launched: 1. whisper_node          — Microphone capture + Whisper transcription 2. gpt4o_planner_node    — GPT-4o task planning 3. action_parser_node    — Grounding + goal dispatch 4. task_executor_server  — ROS 2 action server """


# Declare launch arguments (overridable on CLI) whisper_model_arg = DeclareLaunchArgument( "whisper_model", default_value="large-v3", description="Whisper model size: tiny/base/small/medium/large-v3", ) whisper_device_arg = DeclareLaunchArgument( "whisper_device", default_value="cuda", description="Device for Whisper inference: cuda or cpu", ) gpt_model_arg = DeclareLaunchArgument( "gpt_model", default_value="gpt-4o", description="OpenAI model name for task planning", ) language_arg = DeclareLaunchArgument( "language", default_value="en", description="Language code for Whisper (e.g., en, ar, zh)", ) confidence_threshold_arg = DeclareLaunchArgument( "confidence_threshold", default_value="0.6", description="Minimum Whisper confidence to publish transcription", )


whisper_node = Node( package="voice_pipeline", executable="whisper_node", name="whisper_node", output="screen", parameters=[{ "model_size": LaunchConfiguration("whisper_model"), "device": LaunchConfiguration("whisper_device"), "language": LaunchConfiguration("language"), "confidence_threshold": LaunchConfiguration("confidence_threshold"), }], )


gpt4o_planner_node = Node( package="voice_pipeline", executable="gpt4o_planner_node", name="gpt4o_planner_node", output="screen", parameters=[{ "model": LaunchConfiguration("gpt_model"), "temperature": 0.1, "max_tokens": 1024, }], )


action_parser_node = Node( package="voice_pipeline", executable="action_parser_node", name="action_parser_node", output="screen", )


task_executor_server = Node( package="voice_pipeline", executable="task_executor_server", name="task_executor_server", output="screen", )


return LaunchDescription([ # Arguments whisper_model_arg, whisper_device_arg, gpt_model_arg, language_arg, confidence_threshold_arg, # Startup log LogInfo(msg="Launching Voice-to-Action Pipeline..."), # Nodes whisper_node, gpt4o_planner_node, action_parser_node, task_executor_server, ])

12.9 Chapter Summary and Bridge to Part VI

The pipeline built in this chapter achieves something that would have been a multi-year engineering effort a decade ago: converting spoken natural language into physical robot action using commodity hardware, open-source middleware, and commercial AI APIs. Each stage resolves a distinct problem. Whisper large-v3 handles acoustics — converting noisy microphone audio into reliable text via voice activity detection that avoids unnecessary inference. GPT-4o handles semantics — interpreting that text not merely as syntax to be parsed, but as instruction to be understood, including unstated assumptions about object identity and implicit action sequencing. The action grounding system handles coordinate translation — mapping named references to the 3D poses that MoveIt 2 requires, by querying real-time perception rather than relying on a static world model. The ROS 2 action server handles execution — a preemptible, feedback-reporting layer that recovers from physical failures without requiring human intervention.

The practical result — 1 to 3 seconds from spoken command to first robot movement — positions this system for domestic service tasks where conversational timing is appropriate. The limitations identified in Section 12.7 are real engineering constraints, not caveats added for balance: acoustic noise degrades Whisper, novel objects can cause GPT-4o to hallucinate identities, and the latency floor prevents use in time-critical manipulation contexts where closed-loop reactive control is the correct architecture.

The engineering foundation built across Parts I through V — the ROS 2 architecture, the security layer, the simulation environments, the NVIDIA AI stack, and the VLA pipeline — now makes it possible to ask what all this capability actually means for human life. The remaining chapters change register from implementation to consequence.

Part VI (Chapter 13) examines the concrete benefits that humanoid robots — when properly designed and deployed — can deliver: the physical, economic, and social gains that motivate the enormous investment this field is attracting. Part VII (Chapter 14) then applies equal analytical rigour to the risks: the safety failures, security vulnerabilities, economic disruptions, and ethical questions that must be resolved if those benefits are to be realized without causing equivalent harm.
